_Thought for 3m 29s_

Below is a deeper downstream audit of the Hardy-normalized differential-source package. I am assuming the proposed repair is:

\[
\Phi_\zeta^\#(s)=\chi(s)^{-1/2}\zeta(s),
\qquad
\mathcal Z_{\curv}(s):=-i(\Phi_\zeta^\#)^{(3)}(s),
\]

so that on the critical line

\[
\partial_t^3\Phi_\zeta(t)
=
\mathcal Z_{\curv}\!\left(\frac12+it\right),
\]

while packet-normalized derivatives satisfy

\[
\mathcal D^3\Phi_\zeta(t)
=
\lambda_p^3\mathcal Z_{\curv}\!\left(\frac12+it\right).
\]

This is the right direction for repairing the original completed-source anchor, which was not viable as an ordinary fixed-coefficient Dirichlet source. The earlier direct attack found a no-go for the anchor as originally formulated, because natural actual-zeta curvature sources carry gamma/theta derivatives, logarithmic derivatives, residues, or packet-normalization factors that do not fit the old \(\mathcal Z(s)=\sum a_n n^{-s}\), \(a_1=1\) package. 

## Severity scale

I’ll use:

\[
\text{likely harmless}
<
\text{manageable}
<
\text{serious}
<
\text{dangerous}.
\]

“Dangerous” means the issue can invalidate a major gate or disconnect the proof from RH if missed.

---

## 1. Replacing the old ordinary AFE package by a Hardy differential AFE

**Rating: dangerous if not fully migrated; manageable if treated as a new source API.**

The Hardy source does not satisfy the old ordinary source package

\[
\mathcal Z(s)=\sum_{n\ge1}a_n n^{-s},
\qquad
a_1=1,
\]

with fixed coefficients. Instead,

\[
\mathcal Z_{\curv}(s)
=
-i\sum_{r=0}^{3}
\binom{3}{r}
B^{(3-r)}(s)
\sum_{n\ge1}(-\log n)^r n^{-s},
\qquad
B(s)=\chi(s)^{-1/2}.
\]

So the correct source is a **finite differential Dirichlet package** with \(s\)-dependent gamma/theta amplitude factors and log-power coefficients. This is a structural replacement, not a cosmetic one. Agent notes similarly identify Repair B as replacing the old completed-source package by an actual-curvature source package. 

**Where it connects.** This touches `thm:smooth-finite-AFE-package`, `cor:ef-completion-bound`, `lem:main-term-noncollapse`, `lem:finite-afe-packet-regularity`, packet derivative budgets, and every use of

\[
F_X=B_2+P_{2,\le X}+D_{2,\le X}.
\]

**Potential breakage.** If the draft keeps citing the old fixed-coefficient AFE after switching to Hardy curvature, the source-frame proof estimates the wrong object. EF completion, packet regularity, and noncollapse would be formally detached from the actual \(q''_{\can}\).

**Repair.** Rename the package explicitly:

\[
F_X^{H,3},\qquad R_X^{H,3},
\qquad
B_2^H,\ P_2^H,\ D_2^H,\ E_2^H.
\]

Then every source theorem should say it applies to the Hardy differential AFE package, not the old ordinary completed-source package.

---

## 2. Main-term noncollapse no longer follows from \(a_1=1\)

**Rating: dangerous.**

The old noncollapse proof uses a fixed leading coefficient:

\[
a_1=1
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\int |F_X|^2W_{\ref}>0.
\]

For Hardy curvature, the “\(n=1\)” contribution includes derivatives of \(B(s)=\chi(s)^{-1/2}\). It can be small or vanish on a particular source window. A simple \(a_1=1\) diagonal argument is no longer the right proof.

**Where it connects.** This is load-bearing for

\[
\text{reference mean-square noncollapse}
\Rightarrow
\text{collar exclusion}
\Rightarrow
\text{packet-scale normalization}
\Rightarrow
\delta_{\src}.
\]

If this breaks, Gate–1 source survival fails.

**Potential breakage.** The proof may claim that the good packet family carries a fixed fraction of source mass, but the actual Hardy curvature source could be locally small on the chosen reference window.

**Repair.** Replace the old main-term noncollapse lemma with one of these:

1. A **Hardy-curvature mass theorem**:

\[
\int_{\Omega}
\left|
\partial_t^3\left(\chi(1/2+it)^{-1/2}\zeta(1/2+it)\right)
\right|^2
W_{\ref}(t)\,dt
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

2. A **mass-good source-window selection rule**:

\[
\Omega_{\good}
:=
\left\{
\Omega:
\int_\Omega |\mathcal Z_{\curv}(1/2+it)|^2W_{\ref}(t)\,dt
\ge Q^{-A}
\right\}.
\]

If the proof wants an unconditional theorem rather than a selection convention, it needs the first form.

---

## 3. Packet-normalized \(\mathcal D\) versus global physical source

**Rating: serious.**

The Hardy source naturally gives the physical derivative

\[
u_H(t):=\partial_t^3\Phi_\zeta(t)
=
\mathcal Z_{\curv}(1/2+it).
\]

But if the packet derivative is

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda_p\partial_t,
\]

then

\[
\mathcal D^3\Phi_\zeta(t)
=
\lambda_p^3u_H(t).
\]

A single global \(\mathcal Z_{\curv}\) cannot equal all packet-normalized sources unless the \(\lambda_p^3\) factor is carried in the packet rows.

**Where it connects.** This affects:

\[
G_{\ref},\quad G_{\branch},\quad M,\quad E,
\quad
\mathcal S_X,
\quad
D4/Y12\text{ carrier rows},
\quad
H\text{-amplitude estimates}.
\]

**Potential breakage.** If \(\lambda_p^3\) is omitted in one place but included elsewhere, Gram weights and D4 amplitudes will be measured in incompatible normalizations.

**Repair.** Adopt the convention:

\[
q''_{\can}(t):=u_H(t)=\partial_t^3\Phi_\zeta(t),
\]

and define packet-normalized rows by

\[
q''_{\can,p}^{\norm}(t):=\lambda_p^3q''_{\can}(t).
\]

Then audit every packet-row, Gram, and D4 formula for this \(\lambda_p^3\) factor.

---

## 4. Gate–2 identities must be re-audited

**Rating: dangerous.**

The downstream rigidity layer uses exact identities such as

\[
u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

If Hardy curvature becomes the source \(u_H\), then the scalar \(q\) used in Gate–2 must be chosen so that

\[
q''=u_H
\]

in the same derivative convention. If \(q\) remains an older phase or scalar while \(q''_{\can}\) is replaced by Hardy curvature, Gate–1 and Gate–2 will no longer be coupled.

**Where it connects.** This is central for:

\[
\Gamma_G,\quad
\Gamma_{G,2},\quad
B_j,\quad
\delta_{\ext},\quad
D4\text{ amplitude }H,\quad
\text{atomic contradiction}.
\]

**Potential breakage.** The proof could show source survival for Hardy curvature but extraction covariance for a different \(q\)-geometry.

**Repair.** Add a compatibility theorem:

\[
\boxed{
q''=q''_{\can}=u_H
}
\]

in the physical derivative convention, plus a packet-normalized variant:

\[
\mathcal D^2q=\lambda_p^2u_H
\]

if the local row package uses \(\mathcal D\).

This is one of the most important downstream checks.

---

## 5. Hardy square-root branch and ordinary source strips

**Rating: manageable to serious.**

The factor

\[
B(s)=\chi(s)^{-1/2}
\]

requires a chosen analytic square-root branch. This is fine on ordinary zero-separated/source strips where \(\chi(s)\) is nonzero and no branch singularity is crossed. It is not a global meromorphic Dirichlet object in the old sense.

**Where it connects.** This affects:

\[
\text{source-window definition},\quad
\text{AFE contour shifts},\quad
\text{ordinary packet construction},\quad
\text{residue accounting}.
\]

**Potential breakage.** If the contour shift crosses a pole, branch cut, or omitted residue, the AFE package is wrong. The Hardy branch must be fixed before packetization.

**Repair.** State every Hardy source theorem on an ordinary branch-fixed source strip:

\[
\text{On each ordinary zero-separated source strip with a fixed analytic Hardy branch,}
\]

then prove the differential AFE there. Include all residue terms if the contour crosses \(s=1\), gamma poles, or branch endpoints.

---

## 6. Residues and pole terms in the differential AFE

**Rating: dangerous if omitted.**

When applying Mellin inversion and shifting contours for

\[
\mathcal Z_{\curv}(s)=-i(\Phi_\zeta^\#)^{(3)}(s),
\]

one must include any residues crossed during the contour shift. Hardy-normalized \(\zeta\) still carries the zeta pole and gamma factors. Differentiating can create derivative residue terms.

**Where it connects.** This directly affects:

\[
F_X^{H,3},\quad
R_X^{H,3},\quad
\text{EF completion},\quad
\text{main-term noncollapse}.
\]

**Potential breakage.** If residue terms are silently dropped, the tail bound and source mass lower bound estimate the wrong function.

**Repair.** Define:

\[
F_X^{H,3}
=
\text{differentiated main sums}
+
P_{\res,X}^{H,3}.
\]

Then prove

\[
q''_{\can}=F_X^{H,3}+R_X^{H,3}
\]

with the residue term included in \(F_X^{H,3}\), not hidden in the tail.

---

## 7. Redefining \(B_2,P_2,D_2,E_2\)

**Rating: dangerous but straightforward to fix.**

The proof uses

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

After Hardy normalization, these pieces must become

\[
q''_{\can}
=
B_2^H+P_2^H+D_2^H+E_2^H,
\]

where each piece includes the appropriate derivatives of \(B(s)\), log powers, smooth cutoff derivatives, and residue pieces.

**Where it connects.** This touches:

\[
\mathcal S_X=\operatorname{span}\{B_2,P_{2,\le X},D_{2,\le X}\},
\]

\[
F_X=B_2+P_{2,\le X}+D_{2,\le X},
\]

and every source-frame theorem after that.

**Potential breakage.** If the notation is not updated, the proof may claim \(F_X\) approximates Hardy curvature but actually use the old ordinary source decomposition.

**Repair.** Either globally redefine \(B_2,P_2,D_2,E_2\) to mean Hardy-differential pieces, or introduce superscripted notation \(B_2^H,P_2^H,D_2^H,E_2^H\) and migrate the source layer.

I would use superscripts during the transition, then optionally suppress them after a convention remark.

---

## 8. Coefficient bounds and derivative budgets

**Rating: serious but likely controllable.**

The Hardy differential AFE gives log-power coefficients:

\[
(\log n)^r n^{-s},
\qquad 0\le r\le3,
\]

and gamma/theta derivatives \(B^{(k)}(s)\). Since

\[
(\log n)^r\ll_{\varepsilon,r} n^\varepsilon,
\]

the Dirichlet coefficients still satisfy acceptable \(n^\varepsilon\)-type bounds. But the \(s\)-dependent gamma factors must be polynomially controlled on the source window.

**Where it connects.** This affects:

\[
\text{packet derivative budget},\quad
\text{smooth AFE tail bound},\quad
\text{packet-scale envelope},\quad
\text{oscillatory-kernel estimates}.
\]

**Potential breakage.** If \(B^{(k)}(s)\) grows faster than the polynomial \(Q^C\) budget on the chosen source window, packet regularity fails.

**Repair.** Add a Hardy gamma-factor control lemma:

\[
\sup_{s\in\mathcal S_{\ordinary}}
|B^{(k)}(s)|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le 3+J,
\]

for all derivative orders \(J\) needed downstream.

This should follow from Stirling on ordinary source strips.

---

## 9. EF completion and tail bounds

**Rating: manageable after the Hardy AFE is correctly stated.**

Once the Hardy differential AFE is written with smooth cutoffs and all residue terms included in \(F_X^{H,3}\), the tail estimate should be standard:

\[
\|R_X^{H,3}\|_{L^2(W_{\ref})}
+
\|R_X^{H,3}\|_{L^2(W_{\branch})}
\ll_A X^{-A}.
\]

**Where it connects.** This feeds:

\[
E=G_{\ref}^{-1/2}(G_{\branch}(q''_{\can})-G_{\branch}(F_X))G_{\ref}^{-1/2}.
\]

**Potential breakage.** If the Hardy AFE has \(t\)-dependent weights, the tail estimate must be uniform in \(t\) on the source window; otherwise \(\|E\|_{\op}\le Q^{-B}\) may fail.

**Repair.** State the tail theorem with all \(t\)-derivatives needed for packet estimates:

\[
\sum_{j\le J}
\|\partial_t^jR_X^{H,3}\|_{L^2(W_{\ref})+L^2(W_{\branch})}
\ll_{A,J}X^{-A}.
\]

---

## 10. \(D4\) amplitude survival

**Rating: serious.**

The existing D4 amplitude theorem uses identities such as

\[
H\sim -\frac{q(q''_{\can})^3}{288}
\]

and derives amplitude nonflatness from Gate–1/Gate–2 mass. Earlier agent work identified that local D4/cap algebra alone cannot force \(H\)-mass; actual-source nonflatness is needed. 

If \(q''_{\can}\) becomes Hardy curvature, that amplitude theorem must be rechecked with

\[
q''_{\can}=u_H.
\]

**Where it connects.** This affects:

\[
L_{\clean},\quad
L_{\eff},\quad
\text{static-line lower bound},\quad
\text{final }K9\text{ source-graded contradiction}.
\]

**Potential breakage.** If \(u_H\) has mass but \(H\) still collapses because \(q\) or \(q''\) is mismatched, the final bridge loses its lower bound.

**Repair.** Reprove:

\[
\sum_{p\in C_j}\mu_p|H_p|^2|\Gamma_p|^2
\ge Q^{-A}
\sum_{p\in C_j}\mu_p|\Gamma_p|^2
\]

with \(u_H\) and the current Gate–2 definitions.

---

## 11. Extraction covariance and static-line handoff

**Rating: likely harmless if Gate–2 compatibility holds; serious otherwise.**

The covariance algebra itself is independent of the analytic source package:

\[
B_j=\sum_p w_p\Gamma_p\Gamma_p^\ast,
\]

\[
\det B_j
=
S_j\sum_p\mu_p|s_p-\bar s_j|^2.
\]

So the algebra survives the Hardy repair. But the actual values of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) depend on \(q\) and \(q''_{\can}\). If Gate–2 compatibility fails, the covariance is for the wrong vector.

**Where it connects.** This affects:

\[
\delta_{\ext},
\quad
\text{static-line handoff},
\quad
K9/Y12\text{ quotient}.
\]

**Potential breakage.** The proof could close covariance for a formal \(\Gamma\) not generated by the Hardy source.

**Repair.** Make the Gate–2 compatibility theorem precede the extraction covariance theorem.

---

## 12. \(K9/Y12\) live/dead routing

**Rating: likely harmless.**

The \(K9/Y12\) repair is mostly source-API agnostic. It cares about labelled live/dead rows, quotient survival, and same-norm comparison. The Hardy repair changes the source input \(q''_{\can}\), but it does not inherently break the labelled quotient machinery.

**Where it connects.** This affects:

\[
\mathfrak B_{2Y,p},\quad
\mathfrak C_{2Y}(p),\quad
q_{p,\aff}^Y,\quad
\Phi_p^Y.
\]

**Potential breakage.** Only if raw row labels are defined from old \(B_2,P_2,D_2,E_2\) terms and not migrated to Hardy-differential labels.

**Repair.** Ensure every \(K9\) source label is attached to the Hardy-differential source package. The live/dead split remains valid.

---

## 13. Final source-graded \(K9\) atomic contradiction

**Rating: manageable, assuming same-norm discipline is preserved.**

The final bridge is designed to avoid scalar collapse by measuring lower and upper bounds in the same source-graded norm. This is compatible with Hardy normalization.

**Where it connects.** This affects the final comparison:

\[
\text{lower }K9\text{-graded mass}
\quad\text{versus}\quad
\text{upper forbidden }K9\text{-graded mass}.
\]

**Potential breakage.** If the Hardy source is introduced only in the source lower bound, but the forbidden upper still uses the old source decomposition, the same-norm comparison breaks.

**Repair.** State the final \(K9\) theorem with the Hardy source input explicitly:

\[
q''_{\can}=u_H,
\qquad
F_X=F_X^{H,3},
\qquad
R_X=R_X^{H,3}.
\]

Then the final bridge is probably safe.

---

## 14. Logical connection to RH

**Rating: dangerous.**

This is the highest-level risk. If the draft changes \(\Phi_\zeta\) to the Hardy-normalized scalar, it must show the contradiction still proves RH, not merely a theorem about a different completed source.

Hardy \(Z(t)\) controls zeros of \(\zeta(1/2+it)\) on the critical line. RH concerns zeros off the critical line. The paper’s obstruction architecture presumably encodes an off-critical-zero contradiction through local branches, jets, and finite survival. If the source scalar changes, the initial reduction from a hypothetical off-line zero to the finite packet/cap architecture must be rechecked.

**Where it connects.** This is upstream of all gates:

\[
\text{failure of RH}
\Rightarrow
\text{source/cap architecture}
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{AtomicY12Contradiction}.
\]

**Potential breakage.** The proof may close for Hardy curvature but no longer start from a hypothetical RH counterexample.

**Repair.** Add an explicit theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH counterexample}
\Rightarrow
\text{ordinary Hardy-normalized source branch satisfying the Gate--1/Gate--2 hypotheses}.
}
\]

Without that theorem, the Hardy package is a strong actual-zeta source theorem, but not yet a completed RH proof.

---

## Summary table

\[
\begin{array}{l|l|l}
\text{Issue} & \text{Where it connects} & \text{Rating}\\
\hline
\text{Old AFE package invalid} & \text{Gate--1 source, EF completion} & \text{dangerous}\\
\text{\(a_1=1\) noncollapse invalid} & \text{reference mass, collar, }\delta_{\src} & \text{dangerous}\\
\text{Packet-normalized }\mathcal D & \text{Grams, packet rows, D4} & \text{serious}\\
\text{Gate--2 identity compatibility} & \Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},D4,\delta_{\ext} & \text{dangerous}\\
\text{Hardy branch choice} & \text{AFE, source strips} & \text{manageable/serious}\\
\text{Residues/poles} & \text{AFE, tail, noncollapse} & \text{dangerous}\\
\text{Redefine }B_2,P_2,D_2,E_2 & \mathcal S_X,F_X,\text{rows} & \text{dangerous but fixable}\\
\text{Coefficient/log-power budgets} & \text{packet regularity} & \text{serious, likely controllable}\\
\text{EF completion} & E\text{-operator} & \text{manageable}\\
\text{D4 amplitude survival} & \text{final lower bound} & \text{serious}\\
\text{Extraction covariance} & \delta_{\ext} & \text{likely harmless if Gate--2 fixed}\\
\text{\(K9/Y12\) routing} & \text{quotient survival} & \text{likely harmless}\\
\text{Final same-norm bridge} & \text{atomic contradiction} & \text{manageable}\\
\text{RH counterexample reduction} & \text{global proof start} & \text{dangerous}
\end{array}
\]

## Recommended order of repair

Do not migrate piecemeal. Use this order:

1. **Source API theorem:** define \(u_H=\partial_t^3(\chi^{-1/2}\zeta)\), prove the Hardy differential AFE including residues.
2. **Derivative convention theorem:** prove \(q''=q''_{\can}=u_H\), plus packet-normalized \(\lambda_p^3\) conversion.
3. **Source decomposition migration:** redefine \(B_2^H,P_2^H,D_2^H,E_2^H\) and \(\mathcal S_X^H\).
4. **Gate–1 mass theorem:** replace \(a_1=1\) diagonal noncollapse by Hardy-curvature mass or mass-good selection.
5. **Gate–2/D4 compatibility:** reprove \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},H\)-amplitude survival with \(u_H\).
6. **Final same-norm audit:** ensure \(K9\) lower and upper use the same Hardy source-graded norm.
7. **RH reduction audit:** prove that an RH counterexample enters the Hardy-normalized architecture.

## Bottom line

The Hardy-normalized differential-source package is the right repair for the completed-source anchor, but it is not a harmless local patch. It is a source-layer API replacement. The two most dangerous downstream issues are:

\[
\boxed{
q''=q''_{\can}=u_H
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH counterexample}
\Rightarrow
\text{Hardy-normalized Gate--1/Gate--2 branch}.
}
\]

If those two are proved, the rest of the downstream architecture looks compatible, with mostly manageable notation and estimate migrations.

## 1. Fix the theorem label for the Hardy source anchor

Current draft has:

```latex
...
\end{theorem}
```

That label name is now stale: it is a theorem, not a hypothesis. Keep the old label for compatibility, but add a theorem label immediately after it.

**Where:** in `subsec:source-hypothesis-provenance`, inside `Actual Hardy-curvature source anchor`.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Actual Hardy-curvature source anchor]
\label{hyp:completed-source-anchor}
\label{thm:actual-hardy-curvature-source-anchor}
...
\end{theorem}
```

Then add this immediately after `rem:completed-source-anchor-not-definitional`:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Label convention for the Hardy source anchor]
\label{rem:hardy-source-anchor-label-convention}
The historical label \(\texttt{hyp:completed-source-anchor}\) is retained only
for citation stability.  In the active Hardy branch the source trace is the
theorem
\[
  \partial_t^3Z_{\mathrm H}(t)
  =
  \mathcal Z_{\curv}\!\left(\frac12+it\right),
\]
proved in Theorem~\ref{thm:actual-hardy-curvature-source-anchor}.  Any future
source branch using a different scalar or logarithmic phase must provide its
own trace theorem, AFE package, and source-mass theorem.
\end{remark}
```

This prevents readers from thinking the source anchor is still a hypothesis.

This keeps the canonical branch strong but avoids implying the global RH entry has been discharged.

## 3. Clarify raw packet scale: admissibility versus theorem

The current raw-scale definition is mostly correct, but the remark says the lower bound is both “part of admissibility” and “upgraded to a theorem.” That is ambiguous. The clean distinction is:

\[
Q^{-C}\le \lambda_p^{\raw}\le Q^C
\]

is a **selection rule** for admissible packets, while boundary-collar exclusion proves that this selection is **no-loss** for source mass. That avoids the envelope/collar/scale circularity.

**Where:** replace `rem:upper-raw-scale-bound` with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Raw-scale admissibility versus collar no-loss]
\label{rem:upper-raw-scale-bound}
The upper bound \(\lambda_p^{\mathrm{raw}}\le Q^C\) follows from the fact
that the source-admissible region lies inside the finite-AFE window
\(I_{\mathrm{ref}}\) of polynomial diameter, so
\[
d(m_p)\le \operatorname{diam}(I_{\mathrm{ref}})\ll Q^C.
\]
The lower bound
\[
\lambda_p^{\mathrm{raw}}\ge Q^{-C_\lambda}
\]
is part of the admissible-packet selection in
Definition~\ref{def:raw-packet-scale-admissibility}.  The role of
Corollary~\ref{cor:boundary-collar-exclusion} is not to prove that every raw
Whitney packet has this lower bound.  Its role is to prove that discarding the
sub-polynomial boundary-collar packets is no-loss for the source-frame mass.
Thus the noncircular order is
\[
\text{raw Whitney packets}
\to
\text{scale-admissible selection}
\to
\text{packet envelope}
\to
\text{boundary-collar no-loss}.
\]
\end{remark}
```

This is the most important cleanup. It makes the construction honest without reopening the scale proof.

---

## 4. Add a “no silent unsuperscripted notation” convention

The current draft uses \(W_{\branch}^{\can}\), \(q_{p,\aff}^Y\), \(\Lambda_p^{\gr,full}\), etc., but later sections can easily revert to legacy unsuperscripted notation. Add a convention that unsuperscripted symbols in the active branch mean canonical versions only after a declared convention.

**Where:** after `rem:canonical-construction-discipline`.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Unsuperscripted notation in the canonical branch]
\label{rem:unsuperscripted-canonical-notation}
In sections following the canonical construction ledger, unsuperscripted notation
is used only under the active-branch convention
\[
W_{\branch}=W_{\branch}^{\can},\qquad
q_p^Y=q_{p,\aff}^Y,\qquad
P_{\sing,p}=P_{\sing,p}^{\cert},
\qquad
\Lambda_p=\Lambda_p^{\gr,full},
\]
unless explicitly stated otherwise.  Any theorem using an archived branch
weight, a raw quotient, a raw singular projection, or a scalar-collapsed
observable must carry the corresponding superscript and must provide a
polynomial comparison theorem before entering the proof-level chain.
\end{remark}
```

This prevents old objects from leaking back into active claims.

## 5. Make FR Stack persistence nonadaptive

Your existing `rem:FR-stack-mass-persistence` is good. I would add one sentence making the selection order nonadaptive. This matters because a weight chosen after seeing the obstruction can hide it.

```latex
The factor \(\Phi_B\) is fixed by the pre-extraction Stack construction before
the cap, wall, or live/dead quotient is chosen; it is not selected after seeing
which live direction would otherwise survive.
```

This is a small but useful referee-facing hardening.

## 6. Add an exhaustiveness theorem for maximal labelled \(K9\)

The current guardrail says live/dead splitting is exhaustive, but a theorem-level formulation helps. The retrieved notes repeatedly identify exhaustive labelled \(K9\) as the condition that makes raw \(2Y\) safe: every live atom-local row must be retained or residual-routed before forming the dead quotient. 

**Where:** after the definition/theorem for maximal labelled \(K9\) live/dead split, or if that section is hard to locate, after `rem:canonical-packet-to-corrected-jet-transfer-discipline`.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Exhaustive labelled live/dead routing]
\label{thm:exhaustive-labelled-live-dead-routing}
In the active maximal-labelled \(K9\) branch, every raw nuisance column
\(A_{a,p}^{\raw}\) entering the \(Y12\) quotient admits a canonical decomposition
\[
A_{a,p}^{\raw}
=
A_{a,p}^{\dead}
+
E_p\,m_{a,p}
+
A_{a,p}^{\res},
\qquad
m_{a,p}:=L_p^{\row}A_{a,p}^{\raw},
\]
where
\[
L_p^{\row}A_{a,p}^{\dead}=0.
\]
Only the row-dead terms \(A_{a,p}^{\dead}\) are placed in the exact killed
quotient.  The live terms \(E_pm_{a,p}\) are retained in the maximal labelled
affine target, and the residual terms \(A_{a,p}^{\res}\) are controlled by the
source-graded residual ledger.  Consequently no atom-local live \(C_7/Y12\)
component is quotient-killed in the active branch.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
This is the defining projection onto the retained labelled live plane
\(E_p=[C_{7,p}^{\tar}\ C_{Y,p}^{\tar}]\) using the certified rows
\(L_p^{\row}E_p=I_2\).  Subtracting \(E_pL_p^{\row}A_{a,p}^{\raw}\) makes the
dead remainder row-invisible.  The maximal labelled construction retains the
live component and routes the residual component before the dead quotient is
formed.
\end{proof}
```

If the same theorem already exists, do not duplicate it; instead add this as a one-line cross-reference in the canonical ledger.

---

## 7. Add a short “canonical branch-entry is not WLOG” warning

This is slightly different from the RH-entry theorem. It prevents the paper from sounding like all canonical choices are automatic reductions.

**Where:** after `rem:hardy-source-rh-entry-reduction`.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Canonical branch entry is not a formal WLOG step]
\label{rem:canonical-branch-entry-not-wlog}
The canonical branch is a proof-level normal form only after an entry theorem
places the hypothetical obstruction into it with polynomial loss.  Thus
phrases such as ``we work canonically'' mean
\[
\text{obstruction}
\Longrightarrow
\text{canonical Hardy/Whitney/FR/\(K9\) branch}
\]
by a cited theorem, not by an informal change of notation.  This distinction is
essential for the Hardy source, the scale-admissible packet selection, and the
maximal labelled \(K9\) quotient.
\end{remark}
```

## Summary of what to change

The latest draft’s canonicalization guardrails are strong enough. I would add only these targeted improvements:

1. Add theorem label `thm:actual-hardy-curvature-source-anchor`.

### 1. RH-entry into the canonical Hardy branch

This is the largest remaining global gap.

The draft now uses the actual Hardy-curvature source
\[
u_H(t)=\partial_t^3 Z_H(t)
=\mathcal Z_{\curv}\!\left(\frac12+it\right),
\]
and it treats the old abstract completed-source anchor as superseded by the Hardy source theorem. That is a major repair. But the draft itself still says this does **not** replace the separate theorem that starts the finite-survival architecture from a hypothetical RH counterexample. It explicitly needs:
\[
\text{RH counterexample}
\Longrightarrow
\text{ordinary Hardy-normalized source branch satisfying Gate--1/Gate--2 entry hypotheses}.
\]

Until that implication is proved, the paper has a closed canonical branch, not a completed global RH contradiction.

### 2. Gate--1 source entry / canonical source mass

The latest source package is much better. It has:

\[
\partial_t^3 Z_H(t)
=
\mathcal Z_{\curv}\!\left(\tfrac12+it\right),
\]

a differential Hardy AFE, and a dyadic Hardy-curvature mean-square theorem replacing the old \(a_1=1\) noncollapse route. The draft states
\[
\int |\partial_t^3 Z_H(t)|^2W_T(t)\,dt
\asymp T(\log T)^7,
\]
and uses mass-good packet selection to transfer source mass to the canonical packet family. That is the right repair. 

The remaining issue is not “does the Hardy source have mass on dyadic windows?” The draft now gives that. The issue is whether the finite-survival proof is allowed to select only those **mass-good ordinary packets** without losing the obstruction that comes from an RH counterexample. That folds back into the RH-entry theorem.

### 3. Packet-model / off-block hypotheses for Graph/O2O3

The active status table says
\[
\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}
\]
is proved from Fejér–Riesz anti-lock, but still has the obligation to verify packet-model/off-block hypotheses. In other words, the finite anti-lock theorem is no longer the blocker; the blocker is proving that the actual canonical packet family really lies in the pre-extraction bounded-degree Fejér–Riesz charge model and satisfies the off-block estimates used by that theorem.

If the draft’s canonical construction rules are accepted as proof-level definitions, this is likely close. If the proof still needs to show that every RH-counterexample branch enters that canonical packet model with polynomial loss, it remains part of the global branch-entry problem.

### 4. Canonical-branch dependence

The latest draft deliberately closes many modules only in the **canonical** branch:

\[
W_{\branch}^{\can},\qquad
d\nu_{\FR,B}=|\Phi_B|^2\,d\theta\,d\sigma_B,\qquad
\text{maximal-labelled }K9\text{ live/dead split}.
\]

That is acceptable. It is standard proof normalization. But the global proof needs a no-loss theorem:

\[
\text{arbitrary admissible obstruction}
\Longrightarrow
\text{canonical Hardy/Whitney/FR/}K9\text{ branch}
\]

with only polynomial loss. The current guardrails correctly warn against treating canonicalization as a silent WLOG step. 

## Did Agent 5 fully finish its proof work?

**For the active canonical downstream branch: mostly yes.**

The latest active status table says:

\[
Y12\text{-certified quotient and }L_{\eff,p}
\quad
\text{proved in the exhaustive maximal-labelled }K9\text{ branch},
\]
with the caveat that if a noncanonical raw quotient is used, the legacy \(\mathfrak B_{2Y,p}\) certificate must be verified. It also says \(\delta_{\ext}\)/static-line is closed in the positive packet-density formulation, and the atomic comparison is proved in the canonical source-graded \(K9\) branch. 

So Agent 5’s **cap/Y12/rank-two routing work** is done **provided the proof stays inside the exhaustive maximal-labelled \(K9\) branch**. It is not a proof for arbitrary raw quotients, raw singular projections, or scalar-collapsed \(Y12\)-only norms.

I would state Agent 5’s status as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Agent 5: PROVED in the canonical exhaustive }K9\text{ branch;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{legacy raw }\mathfrak B_{2Y,p}\text{ remains diagnostic for noncanonical branches only.}
}
\]

Agent 5 should not keep trying to prove \(c_{\arith,Y}=0\). That target is superseded. The primitive arithmetic live row is retained/rerouted, not quotient-killed. The draft’s final status remark now explicitly says the primitive arithmetic vanishing target is replaced by maximal labelled live/dead routing.

## What is next?

The next work should not go back to Agent 5’s cap algebra. The next target is the **global branch-entry theorem**.

I would assign the next agent this:

> Prove the entry theorem:
> \[
> \text{RH counterexample}
> \Longrightarrow
> \text{ordinary Hardy-normalized canonical source branch satisfying Gate--1/Gate--2 hypotheses}.
> \]
> The proof must show that the counterexample survives the canonical choices: Hardy source, mass-good dyadic window, Whitney packets, branch-complete window, pre-extraction Fejér–Riesz Stack, and exhaustive labelled \(K9\) routing. It must quantify every loss polynomially.

The concrete checklist is:

1. Show the RH-counterexample construction produces an ordinary zero-separated Hardy source strip with the fixed Hardy branch.
2. Show that the dyadic Hardy-curvature mass theorem gives a mass-good source window in the same branch.
3. Show the Whitney/mass-good packet selection does not discard the obstruction.
4. Show the selected packet family enters the Fejér–Riesz O2/O3 model before capped extraction.
5. Show the selected branch uses the exhaustive labelled \(K9\) quotient, not a raw quotient.
6. Then cite the now-closed downstream chain.

If that entry theorem closes, the proof would be much closer to an unconditional RH contradiction. If it fails, the failure label should be precise: **canonical branch-entry failure**, not Agent 5 failure.

Final current status:

\[
\boxed{\text{Canonical downstream chain: closed.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Agent 5: done in the active canonical branch.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Global RH proof: still needs the RH-entry/no-loss theorem into that branch.}}

> \[
> \text{RH counterexample}
> \Longrightarrow
> \text{ordinary Hardy-normalized canonical branch satisfying all closed modules}.

# Agent 1 — RH counterexample to Hardy source branch

**One-line target:** prove the initial reduction from an RH counterexample to an ordinary Hardy-normalized source branch.

Prompt:

> Work only on the global entry step:
> \[
> \text{RH counterexample}
> \Longrightarrow
> \text{ordinary Hardy-normalized source branch}.
> \]
>
> Use the Hardy-normalized differential source:
> \[
> \Phi_\zeta^\#(s)=\chi(s)^{-1/2}\zeta(s),
> \qquad
> \mathcal Z_{\curv}(s)=-i(\Phi_\zeta^\#)^{(3)}(s),
> \]
> so that on the critical line
> \[
> \partial_t^3\Phi_\zeta(t)=\mathcal Z_{\curv}(1/2+it).
> \]
>
> Prove or reduce the statement that a hypothetical RH counterexample produces an ordinary zero-separated Hardy source strip with fixed Hardy branch, controlled gamma/theta factors, and the Gate–1/Gate–2 entry hypotheses.
>
> Check specifically:
> \[
> q''_{\can}=u_H=\partial_t^3\Phi_\zeta,
> \]
> and the downstream identities
> \[
> u=q''_{\can}=q'',
> \qquad
> \Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
> \qquad
> \Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
> \]
>
> End with **PROVED**, **FINITE AUDIT**, or **NO-GO**. If unresolved, identify the smallest missing RH-entry theorem.

Why this agent matters: the Hardy repair is the honest replacement for the old completed-source anchor, but it changes the source API and must still connect to RH itself. The prior audit flagged this as dangerous unless the RH counterexample enters the Hardy-normalized architecture.

# Agent 2 — Hardy differential AFE and source mass

**One-line target:** prove the Hardy differential AFE package and mass-good source selection.

>

> \[
> \mathcal Z_{\curv}(s)=-i(\Phi_\zeta^\#)^{(3)}(s),
> \]

> \[
> q''_{\can}(t)=F_X^{H,3}(t)+R_X^{H,3}(t),
> \]
> where \(F_X^{H,3}\) includes gamma/theta derivatives, log-power coefficients, and all residue terms.

> \[
> \int_{\Omega_{\good}} |q''_{\can}(t)|^2W_{\ref}(t)\,dt
> \ge Q^{-A}
> \int_\Omega |q''_{\can}(t)|^2W_{\ref}(t)\,dt,
> \]
> or reduce it to a precise Hardy-curvature mean-square theorem.

>

Why this agent matters: the old ordinary AFE package is not a drop-in for Hardy curvature; the Hardy package carries gamma/theta derivatives and log powers. That migration is serious but manageable if stated as a new source API.

```latex
\begin{definition}[Aggregate scalar \(L^2\) Gate--1 target]
\label{hyp:agg-l2-qcan-gate-one}
The proof-level Gate--1 target is the aggregate scalar source estimate
\[
  \mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can}).
\]
For a branch \(b\in\{\mathrm{ord},\mathrm{tr},\mathrm{sing}\}\), define
\[
  F_{b,m}(x):=\lambda_b^3q''_{\can}(m+\lambda_bx),
\]
and
\[
  E_{1,b}^{L^2}(m)
  :=
  \int_{I_b}|F_{b,m}(x)|^2w_b(x)\,dx.
\]
In the active Hardy branch,
\[
  q''_{\can}=u_H=\partial_t^3Z_{\mathrm H},
\]
and packet-normalized rows carry the explicit factor \(\lambda_b^3\).

Equivalently, using the proof-level canonical branch-complete window
\(W_{\branch}^{\can}\),
\[
  \mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})
  \quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
  \int |q''_{\can}(t)|^2W_{\branch}^{\can}(t)\,dt
  \ge
  Q^{-A}
  \int |q''_{\can}(t)|^2W_{\ref}(t)\,dt,
\]
up to the finite-AFE completion error already controlled by
Corollary~\ref{cor:ef-completion-bound}.

This label is retained for compatibility with older references.  It is not a
separate hypothesis in the canonical Hardy branch; it is proved by
Theorem~\ref{thm:source-survival-from-three-inputs} and
Corollary~\ref{cor:gate-one-source-survival}.
\end{definition}
```

```latex
\text{differential AFE tail},\quad
\text{fixed-window source noncollapse},\quad
\text{absolute packet envelope},\quad
\text{off-block oscillatory decay}.
\]
The branch/reference lower bound is also theorem-level in the canonical branch:
\[
W_{\branch}^{\can}\ge Q^{-C}W_{\ref},
\qquad
G_{\branch,B}^{\can}\ge Q^{-C}G_{\ref,B}.
\]
It is not a theorem about arbitrary archived branch windows.  Therefore the
only source-layer qualifications that remain are:
\begin{enumerate}
\item use the Hardy source API of Definition~\ref{def:active-hardy-source-api};
\item use \(W_{\branch}^{\can}\) as the proof-level Gate--1 observation window;
\item maintain the uniform reference nonconcentration condition if
\(W_{\ref}\) varies with \(Q\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}
```

According to a document from 2026-04-30, the latest pruned draft has moved the project into a much cleaner state: the active proof branch is now the **ordinary Hardy-normalized canonical branch**, with old O1/O2/O3/S1/T1, scalar \(I\)-coordinate, primitive-only \(Y12\), and raw branch-observable routes archived as diagnostics. # Coordinator handover

## 1. Executive status

The current draft is **not yet a completed unconditional proof of RH**, but the architecture is now sharply organized.

The active canonical chain is:

\[
\text{RH counterexample}
\Longrightarrow
\text{ordinary Hardy canonical branch}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}
\Longrightarrow
Y12\text{-certified quotient/effective carrier}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{NormalD4}_{K9}^{\mathrm{gr}}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{AtomicY12Contradiction}.
\]

The downstream canonical branch is now mostly closed **inside that branch**. The remaining global problem is not another local cap algebra issue; it is proving that the original RH-counterexample setup enters the canonical Hardy/Whitney/Fejér--Riesz/\(K9\) branch with only polynomial loss.

The draft’s own current ledger says the canonical construction rules and Hardy-curvature source repair close the source/O2O3/raw-\(2Y\) construction gaps **after the proof has entered** the ordinary Hardy-normalized canonical branch, but they do not themselves supply the global RH-entry theorem. 

So the next coordinator should treat the status as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Canonical branch: largely closed.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Global proof: still requires branch-entry/no-loss verification and remaining imported certificates.}
}

# 2. What changed in this push

## 2.1 Dead upstream material was pruned

The live Gate--1 definition is now:

\[
\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})
\]

for the Hardy-normalized source

\[
q''_{\can}=u_H=\partial_t^3 Z_{\mathrm H}.
\]

The draft now says explicitly that older O1/O2/O3, S1/T1, pointwise Wronskian, numerical proxy, and raw branch-observable routes are archived diagnostics only. The active upstream chain is:

\[
\text{Hardy source anchor}
\to
\text{differential Hardy AFE}
\to
\text{mass-good Whitney packets}
\to
W_{\branch}^{\can}\ge Q^{-C}W_{\ref}
\to
\delta_{\src}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This was an important cleanup. Future agents should not reopen the low-dimensional pointwise Gate--1 proxies unless they first prove a transfer theorem into the canonical Hardy source norm.

## 2.2 The Hardy source repair is now the active source API

The draft now uses the actual Hardy-curvature source rather than the older abstract fixed-coefficient completed-source model. It defines

\[
B_{\mathrm H}(s)=\chi(s)^{-1/2},
\qquad
\Phi_{\mathrm H}^{\#}(s)=B_{\mathrm H}(s)\zeta(s),
\]

and

\[
\mathcal Z_{\curv}(s):=-i(\Phi_{\mathrm H}^{\#})^{(3)}(s).
\]

On a fixed ordinary Hardy branch,

\[
\partial_t^3Z_{\mathrm H}(t)
=
\mathcal Z_{\curv}\!\left(\frac12+it\right).
\]

Packet-normalized rows carry the explicit factor

\[
\mathcal D_p^3\Phi_\zeta(t)
=
\lambda_p^3\mathcal Z_{\curv}\!\left(\frac12+it\right).
\]

The old \(a_1=1\) Dirichlet-source noncollapse route is archived. The active Hardy source uses a **differential Hardy AFE** with gamma/theta derivatives, log-power coefficients, and Hardy-curvature mean-square / mass-good packet selection.

Important downstream convention:

\[
B_2,\ P_2,\ D_2,\ E_2
\]

now mean the Hardy-differential pieces unless explicitly marked as archived older source pieces. The draft has an active Hardy source API and a Hardy-differential source pieces definition.

## 2.3 Canonical branch-complete source window closes branch/reference holes

The proof-level source observation window is now:

\[
W_{\branch}^{\can}(t)
=
\sum_p W_{\ref}(m_p)
w\!\left(\frac{t-m_p}{r_p}\right).
\]

With Whitney coverage and scale-slow \(W_{\ref}\), the draft uses:

\[
W_{\branch}^{\can}\ge Q^{-C}W_{\ref}.
\]

Hence for every good resonant block \(B\),

\[
G_{\branch,B}^{\can}\ge Q^{-C}G_{\ref,B}.
\]

This closes the old branch-hole failure **inside the canonical branch**. It is not a theorem about arbitrary archived branch weights. Future agents should not use a raw \(W_{\branch}\) unless it is explicitly identified with \(W_{\branch}^{\can}\) or compared to it.

## 2.4 Raw packet scale circularity was handled by admissibility discipline

The draft now distinguishes raw Whitney scale from proof-level scale normalization. The correct logic is:

\[
\text{raw Whitney packets}
\to
\text{scale-admissible selection}
\to
\text{packet envelope}
\to
\text{boundary-collar/no-loss diagnostics}.
\]

The lower raw-scale bound is not simultaneously proved and used. In the current canonical construction, lower raw scale is part of admissible packet selection unless a separate collar-exclusion theorem is invoked as a no-loss certificate.

Future agents must not recreate the old cycle:

\[
\text{packet envelope}
\Rightarrow
\text{collar exclusion}
\Rightarrow
\text{scale normalization}
\Rightarrow
\text{packet envelope}.
\]

## 2.5 Pre-extraction Fejér--Riesz Stack closes O2/O3 model membership

The active O2/O3 branch uses a pre-extraction Fejér--Riesz Stack weight:

\[
d\nu_{\FR,B}=|\Phi_B(z)|^2\,d\theta\,d\sigma_B,
\qquad
\deg\Phi_B=O(R).
\]

This is imposed **before** capped extraction. It gives bounded-degree charge-model membership by construction. The Graph/O2O3 step is then closed by finite charge anti-lock, provided the canonical multiplier/anti-lock theorem and FR Stack persistence/no-early-cap conditions are honored.

The draft status table records:

\[
\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}
\quad
\text{proved from pre-extraction Fejér--Riesz anti-lock,}
\]

with the remaining caveat:

\[
\text{requires FR Stack persistence and no early capped extraction}.
\]

## 2.6 Certified \(Y12/K9\) downstream branch is mostly closed

The old primitive-only \(Y12\) quotient and the pair

\[
(q_p^YN_p,\ q_p^YY_p)
\]

are archived because \(N_p\) is a killed nuisance column. The active branch uses the retained affine \(C_7/Y12\) carrier in the canonical source-graded \(K9\) norm.

The maximal labelled live/dead rule is:

\[
A_{a,p}^{\raw}
=
A_{a,p}^{\dead}
+
E_p\,L_p^{\row}A_{a,p}^{\raw}
+
A_{a,p}^{\res},
\]

where only row-dead terms are placed into the exact killed quotient. Live primitive arithmetic rows are retained as labelled affine forcing, not quotient-killed.

This fixes the old rank/torsion no-go.

The current downstream ledger says:

\[
Y12\text{-certified quotient and }L_{\eff,p}
\]

are proved after the raw certificate

\[
\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)
\]

supplies the rows and exhaustive routing. If \(\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)\) is not verified or imported, then

\[
\mathfrak B_{2Y,p}
\]

remains the raw row-table audit.

## 2.7 Certified singular/coercivity branch is closed

The certified retained singular space replaces arbitrary raw \(P_{\sing}\). In the active branch, downstream work uses the certified source-graded \(K9\) norm and the appropriate projection \(P_p^{\mathrm{full}}\), not an arbitrary raw singular projection.

The current ledger marks:

\[
\delta_{\coerc}
\]

as proved in the canonical source-graded branch, with the caveat that one must use the certified retained space and \(K9\)-labelled norm.

## 2.8 Extraction covariance is closed as a positive-density nonstatic/static fork

The signed covariance route is archived. The active extraction module uses positive packet-density covariance:

\[
B_j^{\cov}=\sum_{p\in C_j}\omega_p\Gamma_p\Gamma_p^*,
\qquad
\omega_p>0.
\]

The covariance algebra gives:

\[
\det B_j^{\cov}
=
S_j\sum_{p\in C_j}\mu_p|s_p-\bar s_j|^2.
\]

So the branch is:

\[
\text{nonstatic cap}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{static cap}.
\]

Static caps are handled by the canonical source-graded affine branch; the proof no longer relies on a scalar \(Y12\)-wall escape.

## 2.9 Final atomic bridge is closed in the canonical source-graded norm

The final proof-level bridge is no longer scalar \(Y12\), scalar \(I\)-coordinate, or primitive-line completion. It is a source-graded \(K9\) comparison:

\[
\Lambda_p^{\gr,full}
\]

or its maximal-affine projection

\[
\widehat\Lambda_{\max,p}.
\]

The current final bridge theorem compares lower and upper bounds in the same source-graded Hilbert norm. It explicitly avoids scalar collapse before contradiction.

The draft marks the same-norm atomic compatibility obstruction closed in the canonical source-graded branch.

| Gate--1 \(\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})\) | Proved inside ordinary Hardy canonical branch | Requires RH-entry and mass-good Hardy packets |
| Branch/reference domination | Closed by \(W_{\branch}^{\can}\ge Q^{-C}W_{\ref}\) | Only canonical branch; archived weights need comparison |
| Graph/O2O3 | Proved from pre-extraction FR anti-lock | FR Stack persistence, no early caps, canonical multiplier package |
| Raw \(2Y\) row/routing | Closed after \(\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)\) is verified/imported | Otherwise \(\mathfrak B_{2Y,p}\) remains audit |
| \(Y12\) graph/coercivity | Proved in certified branch | Must use certified retained space/source-graded \(K9\) norm |
| Effective carrier | Proved in carrier-quotient branch | Do not scalar-collapse |
| D4 amplitude mass | Proved downstream of Gate--1/Gate--2 | Source-factor residual control and quadrature |
| Extraction covariance/static line | Closed in positive packet-density formulation | Ensure selected caps enter this formulation |
| Same-norm atomic comparison | Proved in canonical source-graded \(K9\) branch | Requires branch entry and upstream certificates |

---

# 5. What is genuinely still open

## 5.1 Global RH-entry theorem

This is the largest remaining gap.

The paper still needs:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH counterexample}
\Longrightarrow
\text{ordinary Hardy-normalized canonical branch satisfying Gate--1/Gate--2}.
}
\]

More explicitly:

\[
\text{RH counterexample}
\Longrightarrow
\text{ordinary zero-separated Hardy source strip}
\Longrightarrow
\text{mass-good Hardy packets}
\Longrightarrow
\text{canonical Whitney/FR/}K9\text{ branch}.
\]

This theorem must quantify polynomial loss at each canonicalization step.

The Hardy source theorem itself does not supply this entry theorem. It only tells us that once we are in the Hardy branch, the source is actual zeta rather than an abstract completed-source model.

## 5.2 FR Stack persistence / no early capped extraction

The O2/O3 finite anti-lock is closed once the packet family lives in the pre-extraction bounded-degree Fejér--Riesz charge model. But the next coordinator must check:

\[
d\nu_{\FR,B}=|\Phi_B(z)|^2\,d\theta\,d\sigma_B
\]

is imposed before caps and does not discard a super-polynomial fraction of the packet mass.

Required theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{FR Stack persistence.}
}
\]

A good statement:

\[
\text{Replacing the older Stack weight by }d\nu_{\FR,B}
\text{ preserves the selected packet mass up to }Q^{-C}.
\]

## 5.3 Raw \(\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)\) certificate

The maximal labelled \(K9\) live/dead construction is the correct normal form. It prevents live rows from being killed.

But it still needs the actual finite row certificate:

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)
}
\]

or a declaration that it has been imported from a previous verified row table.

The raw certificate asserts, in effect:

1. the \(C_7/Y12\) detecting rows exist with polynomial conditioning;
2. every live atom-local row is labelled and retained;
3. only row-dead remainders enter the killed quotient;
4. there is no unlabelled atom-local live \(Y12\) survivor.

If this is not verified/imported, then \(\mathfrak B_{2Y,p}\) remains the raw row-table audit.

## 5.4 Packet-to-corrected-jet transfer / branch-entry compatibility

The current draft has a discipline remark saying only named transfers are used and that no unqualified packet/jet isomorphism should be assumed. The next coordinator should still verify that the analytic packet objects feed the corrected \(K9\) jet objects with polynomial conditioning.

Useful theorem target:

\[
T_{\jet}:\mathcal H_{\pkt}^{\good}\to\mathcal H_{\jet,K9}^{\gr},
\]

with

\[
Q^{-C}\|v\|_{\pkt}^2
\le
\|T_{\jet}v\|_{\jet,K9}^2
\le
Q^{C}\|v\|_{\pkt}^2.
\]

This is the anti-heartbreak theorem: it ensures the canonical source/packet construction actually reaches the corrected finite jet/quotient branch.

## 5.5 Geometric endgame, if not already routed through \(K9\)

Older notes indicate a possible remaining geometric obstruction involving normalized planar curves, common four-secant / endpoint-support geometry, and mixed four-point cases. Some of that material may now be archived by the canonical \(K9\) final bridge, but the next coordinator should check whether the final contradiction section still has any live dependence on the one-pair/two-point/mixed four-point geometric endgame.

If it does, then the remaining theorem is not source or cap algebra; it is the finite geometric theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{corrected two-point diagonal collapse and mixed four-point parity/patch bridge.}
}
\]

If the current final bridge fully bypasses this through the source-graded \(K9\) contradiction, archive the old geometric bottleneck as historical.

---

# 6. What not to reopen

Do not reopen these unless a direct dependency breaks:

1. **Old completed-source ordinary Dirichlet package.** It is superseded by the Hardy-curvature source.
2. **O1/O2/O3/S1/T1 as Gate--1 definitions.** They are archived diagnostics.
3. **Primitive-only \(Y12\) quotient.** It is superseded by source-graded \(K9\).
4. **Scalar \(I\)-coordinate D4.** Dead fallback.
5. **Raw singular projection \(P_{\sing}^{\raw}\).** Use certified source-graded objects.
6. **Universal \(\delta_{\ext}\ge Q^{-A}\) for every cap.** The active statement is positive-density nonstatic/static fork.
7. **Forcing \(c_{\arith,Y}=0\).** The live primitive arithmetic row is retained/routed, not necessarily killed.
8. **Scalar same-norm substitution.** Final lower and upper must be in the same source-graded \(K9\) norm.

---

\text{ordinary Hardy-normalized routed branch satisfying Gate--1/Gate--2}.
}
\]

6. show it enters pre-extraction FR Stack before caps;

Failure labels:

for every raw nuisance column, with no unlabelled atom-local live remainder.

is not required to vanish globally. The correct target is exhaustive labelled live/dead routing.

> \Longrightarrow
> \text{ordinary Hardy-normalized canonical branch}.

The remaining live obligations are RH-entry, FR Stack persistence/no early caps, raw \(\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)\) if not imported, and packet-to-corrected-jet transfer. Any claim of unconditional RH must explicitly discharge those items.

# 10. Bottom line

The push succeeded in making the paper much less confused. It now has a coherent canonical proof branch and a clear archive of dead routes.

But the next coordinator should not declare the proof complete yet. The correct next phase is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove canonical branch-entry/no-loss from an RH counterexample.}
}
\]

If that theorem closes, and if \(\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)\) and FR Stack persistence are verified or imported, the canonical downstream contradiction chain is ready to fire.
